# Kafka Connect REST API v1 to v2 Migration

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Kafka Connect REST API: the v1 connector resource handlers, the v2 connector resource handlers, and the version routing logic. Identify what changed between v1 and v2 in the task status and error response schemas.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],

    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

   100→    private List<Plugin<ConnectRestExtension>> connectRestExtensionPlugins = Collections.emptyList();
   101→
   102→    /**
   103→     * Create a REST server for this herder using the specified configs.
   104→     */
   105→    protected RestServer(RestServerConfig config) {
   106→        this.config = config;
   107→
   108→        List<String> listeners = config.listeners();
   109→        List<String> adminListeners = config.adminListeners();
   110→
   111→        jettyServer = new Server();
   112→        handlers = new ContextHandlerCollection();
   113→        requestTimeout = new RequestTimeout(DEFAULT_REST_REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS, DEFAULT_HEALTH_CHECK_TIMEOUT_MS);
   114→
   115→        createConnectors(listeners, adminListeners);
   116→    }
   117→
   118→    /**
   119→     * Adds Jetty connector for each configured listener
   120→     */
   121→    public final void createConnectors(List<String> listeners, List<String> adminListeners) {
   122→        List<Connector> connectors = new ArrayList<>();
   123→
   124→        for (String listener : listeners) {
   125→            Connector connector = createConnector(listener);
   126→            connectors.add(connector);
   127→            log.info("Added connector for {}", listener);
   128→        }
   129→
   130→        jettyServer.setConnectors(connectors.toArray(new Connector[0]));
   131→
   132→        if (adminListeners != null && !adminListeners.isEmpty()) {
   133→            for (String adminListener : adminListeners) {
   134→                Connector conn = createConnector(adminListener, true);
   135→                jettyServer.addConnector(conn);
   136→                log.info("Added admin connector for {}", adminListener);
   137→            }
   138→        }
   139→    }

    public ConnectorStateInfo connectorStatus(String connName) {
        ConnectorStatus connector = statusBackingStore.get(connName);
        if (connector == null)
            throw new NotFoundException("No status found for connector " + connName);

        Collection<TaskStatus> tasks = statusBackingStore.getAll(connName);

        ConnectorStateInfo.ConnectorState connectorState = new ConnectorStateInfo.ConnectorState(
                connector.state().toString(), connector.workerId(), connector.trace(), connector.version());
        List<ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState> taskStates = new ArrayList<>();

        for (TaskStatus status : tasks) {
            taskStates.add(new ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState(status.id().task(),
                    status.state().toString(), status.workerId(), status.trace(), status.version()));
        }

        Collections.sort(taskStates);

        Map<String, String> conf = rawConfig(connName);
        return new ConnectorStateInfo(connName, connectorState, taskStates, connectorType(conf));
    }
--
    public ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState taskStatus(ConnectorTaskId id) {
        TaskStatus status = statusBackingStore.get(id);

        if (status == null)
            throw new NotFoundException("No status found for task " + id);

        return new ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState(id.task(), status.state().toString(),
                status.workerId(), status.trace(), status.version());
    }

## Exploration Report: Kafka Connect REST API Implementation

### Summary
After exploring the Kafka Connect REST API codebase in `/workspace/kafka--0753c489/connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest`, I found that **the current implementation does NOT use separate v1 and v2 API versions**. Instead, there is a single unified REST API with version-agnostic endpoints.

### Key Findings

#### 1. **Single Resource Handlers (No V1/V2 Separation)**
The implementation uses unified resource handler classes without version-specific variants:
- **ConnectorsResource.java** (`/workspace/kafka--0753c489/connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/ConnectorsResource.java`)
  - Handles all connector operations: create, get, delete, status, config, tasks, restart, pause, resume, offsets
  - Uses @Path("/connectors") without version prefix
  
- **ConnectorPluginsResource.java** (`/workspace/kafka--0753c489/connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/ConnectorPluginsResource.java`)
  - Uses @Path("/connector-plugins") without version prefix
  - Supports plugin versioning via query parameter `?version=latest`

- **RootResource.java** (`/workspace/kafka--0753c489/connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/RootResource.java`)
  - Uses @Path("/") for root endpoints
  - Server info and health check endpoints

- **InternalClusterResource.java** and **InternalConnectResource.java**
  - Internal endpoints for inter-worker communication
  - No version separation

#### 2. **Unified Schema Classes (No V1/V2 Variants)**

184-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the analysis of the Kafka Connect REST API implementation. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I explored the Kafka Connect REST API in the Apache Kafka repository (`apache/kafka`) and identified the complete implementation structure. **Important finding**: The current implementation uses a **single unified REST API** with **no separate v1 and v2 versions**.

### Key Files Found:

**Resource Handlers:**
- `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/ConnectorsResource.java` - Main connector operations handler
- `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/ConnectorPluginsResource.java` - Plugin and version management
- `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/RootResource.java` - Server info and health check

**Response Schemas:**
- `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/ConnectorStateInfo.java` - Task status schema (contains TaskState and ConnectorState)
- `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/ErrorMessage.java` - Error response schema
- `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/Message.java` - Success response schema

**Version Routing:**
- `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/ConnectRestServer.java` - REST server configuration and resource registration
- Version routing exists only for **connector plugins** via query parameters (e.g., `?version=latest`), not for API endpoint versioning

The analysis has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details about all relevant files, symbols, and the explanation of how the REST API is structured.

Returns ConnectorStateInfo for status endpoints\\n\\n2. **ConnectorPluginsResource.java** - Handles plugin and version management:\\n   - @Path(\\\"/connector-plugins\\\")\\n   - Contains version routing logic via `getConnectorConfigDef()` method with @QueryParam(\\\"version\\\") parameter\\n   - Uses VersionRange from org.apache.maven.artifact.versioning to handle plugin version specifications\\n   - Supports version parameter format like \\\"latest\\\", \\\"1.0\\\", \\\"[1.0,2.0)\\\", etc.\\n\\n3. **RootResource.java** - Server info and health check endpoints\\n   - @Path(\\\"/\\\") - root endpoints\\n   - serverInfo() - returns kafka cluster ID\\n   - healthCheck() - worker readiness check\\n\\n4. **InternalConnectResource.java and InternalClusterResource.java** - Internal inter-worker communication\\n   - Used for cluster-internal requests\\n   - putTaskConfigs(), fenceZombies(), etc.\\n\\n5. **LoggingResource.java** - Admin logging configuration\\n\\n### Task Status and Error Response Schemas\\n\\n1. **ConnectorStateInfo.java** - Main task status schema:\\n   - Contains ConnectorState and TaskState nested classes\\n   - TaskState extends AbstractState with fields: id, state, worker_id, trace, version (where version is connector plugin version)\\n   - JSON format includes fields: \\\"id\\\", \\\"state\\\", \\\"worker_id\\\", \\\"msg\\\", \\\"version\\\"\\n   - No separate v1/v2 implementations\\n\\n2. **ErrorMessage.java** - Unified error response schema:\\n   - Fields: error_code (int), message (String)\\n   - JSON fields: \\\"error_code\\\", \\\"message\\\"\\n   - Single implementation for all API errors\\n   - Generated automatically by ConnectExceptionMapper\\n\\n3. **Message.java** - Standard success response schema:\\n   - Single field: message (String)\\n   - Used for successful operations like alter offsets, reset offsets\\n\\n### Version Routing Logic\\n\\nVersion routing exists only at the **connector plugin level**, not at the API endpoint level:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorPluginsResource.getConnectorConfigDef()** (line 156-169):\\n   ```java\\n   public List<ConfigKeyInfo> getConnectorConfigDef(\\n       final @PathParam(\\\"pluginName\\\") String pluginName,\\n       final @QueryParam(\\\"version\\\") @DefaultValue(\\\"latest\\\") String version)\\n   ```\\n   - Parses version parameter using PluginUtils.connectorVersionRequirement()\\n   - Creates VersionRange object\\n   - Forwards to herder.connectorPluginConfig() with version requirement\\n\\n2. **ConnectRestServer.java** - Resource registration:\\n   - regularResources() returns: RootResource, ConnectorsResource, InternalConnectResource, ConnectorPluginsResource\\n   - Single set of resources registered with no version alternatives\\n   - registerRestExtensions() hook for custom REST extension plugins\\n\\n### AbstractStatus Class\\n\\n**AbstractStatus.java** - Base class for status objects:\\n- Fields: id, state, workerId, generation, trace, version\\n- The 'version' field refers to connector/plugin version, not API version\\n- Used by both TaskStatus and ConnectorStatus for consistent schema\\n\\n### Key Findings\\n\\n1. **No v1/v2 API separation**: The REST API uses a single unified version without separate v1 and v2 endpoint paths (no /v1/connectors or /v2/connectors)\\n\\n2. **No content negotiation for API versioning**: No Accept header processing or media-type versioning for different API versions\\n\\n3. **Version parameter for plugins only**: The only version parameter is for connector/plugin configuration definitions, not for API endpoints themselves\\n\\n4. **Unified schemas**: Task status (ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState) and error responses (ErrorMessage) use single implementations across the entire API\\n\\n5. **Internal clustering**: Inter-worker communication uses the same API handlers (InternalConnectResource extends ConnectorsResource) with internal request signatures for authentication\\n\\nThe Kafka Connect REST API architecture prioritizes backward compatibility through schema stability and connector plugin versioning, rather than maintaining separate API versions.\"\n}\n",
